<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lewis_Hamilton_2016_Malaysia_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Lewis_Hamilton_2016_Malaysia_2.jpg/150px-Lewis_Hamilton_2016_Malaysia_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Lewis_Hamilton_2016_Malaysia_2.jpg/225px-Lewis_Hamilton_2016_Malaysia_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Lewis_Hamilton_2016_Malaysia_2.jpg/300px-Lewis_Hamilton_2016_Malaysia_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lewis_Hamilton_2016_Malaysia_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lewis_Hamilton" title="Lewis Hamilton">Lewis Hamilton</a> is the defending champion and the current World Championship leader.</div></div></div>
<p>The <b>2020 FIA Formula One World Championship</b> is a motor racing championship for <a href="/wiki/Formula_One_cars" class="mw-redirect" title="Formula One cars">Formula One cars</a> which marks the 70th anniversary of the <a href="/wiki/1950_Formula_One_season" title="1950 Formula One season">first Formula One season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup> The championship is recognised by the governing body of international <a href="/wiki/Motorsport" title="Motorsport">motorsport</a>, the <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9d%C3%A9ration_Internationale_de_l%27Automobile" title="Fédération Internationale de l&#39;Automobile">Fédération Internationale de l'Automobile</a> (FIA), as the highest class of competition for <a href="/wiki/Open-wheel_car" title="Open-wheel car">open-wheel racing cars</a>. Drivers and teams are scheduled to compete for the titles of <a href="/wiki/List_of_Formula_One_World_Drivers%27_Champions" title="List of Formula One World Drivers&#39; Champions">World Drivers' Champion</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Formula_One_World_Constructors%27_Champions" title="List of Formula One World Constructors&#39; Champions">World Constructors' Champion</a> respectively.
</p><p>The championship was originally due to start in March,<sup id="cite_ref-original_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-original-3">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> but was postponed until July in response to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>. The season was due to be contested over a record of 22 <a href="/wiki/Formula_One#Grands_Prix" title="Formula One">Grands Prix</a>, but as some races have been cancelled and new races were added to replace them, a total of 17 races were confirmed to be run.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The season started in July with the <a href="/wiki/2020_Austrian_Grand_Prix" title="2020 Austrian Grand Prix">Austrian Grand Prix</a><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> and will end in December with the <a href="/wiki/2020_Abu_Dhabi_Grand_Prix" class="mw-redirect" title="2020 Abu Dhabi Grand Prix">Abu Dhabi Grand Prix</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Lewis_Hamilton" title="Lewis Hamilton">Lewis Hamilton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_in_Formula_One" title="Mercedes-Benz in Formula One">Mercedes</a> are the reigning World Drivers' and World Constructors' champions respectively, after they both won their sixth championship in 2019.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Free_practice_drivers">Free practice drivers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2020_Formula_One_World_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Free practice drivers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Across the season, three drivers drove as a test or third driver in free practice sessions. <a href="/wiki/Jack_Aitken" title="Jack Aitken">Jack Aitken</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roy_Nissany" title="Roy Nissany">Roy Nissany</a> both drove for <a href="/wiki/Williams_Grand_Prix_Engineering" title="Williams Grand Prix Engineering">Williams</a> at one and two Grands Prix respectively, while <a href="/wiki/Robert_Kubica" title="Robert Kubica">Robert Kubica</a> drove for <a href="/wiki/Alfa_Romeo_in_Formula_One" title="Alfa Romeo in Formula One">Alfa Romeo Racing</a> at three Grands Prix.<sup id="cite_ref-entry_lists_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-entry_lists-30">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Team_changes">Team changes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2020_Formula_One_World_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Team changes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Red_Bull_GmbH" title="Red Bull GmbH">Red Bull GmbH</a>, the parent company of <a href="/wiki/Red_Bull_Racing" title="Red Bull Racing">Red Bull Racing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scuderia_Toro_Rosso" title="Scuderia Toro Rosso">Scuderia Toro Rosso</a>, renamed Toro Rosso as "<a href="/wiki/Scuderia_AlphaTauri" title="Scuderia AlphaTauri">Scuderia AlphaTauri</a>". The team uses the constructor name "AlphaTauri".<sup id="cite_ref-:2_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-25">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The name is derived from Red Bull's <a href="/wiki/AlphaTauri_(fashion_brand)" title="AlphaTauri (fashion brand)">AlphaTauri fashion brand</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Driver_changes">Driver changes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2020_Formula_One_World_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Driver changes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After a year's absence, <a href="/wiki/Esteban_Ocon" title="Esteban Ocon">Esteban Ocon</a> returned to racing in Formula One after signing a contract with <a href="/wiki/Renault_in_Formula_One" title="Renault in Formula One">Renault</a>, replacing <a href="/wiki/Nico_H%C3%BClkenberg" title="Nico Hülkenberg">Nico Hülkenberg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ocon_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ocon-32">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Kubica" title="Robert Kubica">Robert Kubica</a> left <a href="/wiki/Williams_Grand_Prix_Engineering" title="Williams Grand Prix Engineering">Williams</a> at the end of the 2019 championship and joined <a href="/wiki/Alfa_Romeo_in_Formula_One" title="Alfa Romeo in Formula One">Alfa Romeo Racing</a> as a reserve driver.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Latifi" title="Nicholas Latifi">Nicholas Latifi</a>, the <a href="/wiki/2019_Formula_2_Championship" title="2019 Formula 2 Championship">2019 Formula 2 Championship</a> runner-up, replaced Kubica at Williams.<sup id="cite_ref-Latifi_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Latifi-33">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kubica_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kubica-34">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mid-season_changes">Mid-season changes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2020_Formula_One_World_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Mid-season changes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A day before the <a href="/wiki/2020_British_Grand_Prix" title="2020 British Grand Prix">British Grand Prix</a> weekend, <a href="/wiki/Racing_Point_F1_Team" title="Racing Point F1 Team">Racing Point</a> driver <a href="/wiki/Sergio_P%C3%A9rez" title="Sergio Pérez">Sergio Pérez</a> tested positive for the <a href="/wiki/Severe_acute_respiratory_syndrome_coronavirus_2" title="Severe acute respiratory syndrome coronavirus 2">SARS-2 coronavirus</a> and was ruled out of the race weekend.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> After seeking clarification from <a href="/wiki/Public_Health_England" title="Public Health England">Public Health England</a>, Racing Point stated that they intended to let Pérez race in the <a href="/wiki/70th_Anniversary_Grand_Prix" title="70th Anniversary Grand Prix">70th Anniversary Grand Prix</a> pending a negative SARS-2 coronavirus test.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> This re-test came back positive and so Pérez was also unable to take part in the 70th Anniversary Grand Prix. He was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Nico_H%C3%BClkenberg" title="Nico Hülkenberg">Nico Hülkenberg</a> for both races, who had raced for the team's predecessor <a href="/wiki/Force_India" title="Force India">Force India</a> in <a href="/wiki/2012_Formula_One_World_Championship" title="2012 Formula One World Championship">2012</a> and from <a href="/wiki/2014_Formula_One_World_Championship" title="2014 Formula One World Championship">2014</a> to <a href="/wiki/2016_Formula_One_World_Championship" title="2016 Formula One World Championship">2016</a>, and last raced in Formula One at the <a href="/wiki/2019_Abu_Dhabi_Grand_Prix" title="2019 Abu Dhabi Grand Prix">2019 Abu Dhabi Grand Prix</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Pérez had a negative SARS-2 coronavirus test result the week preceding the <a href="/wiki/2020_Spanish_Grand_Prix" title="2020 Spanish Grand Prix">Spanish Grand Prix</a> weekend and he competed in the Grand Prix having been cleared by the <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9d%C3%A9ration_Internationale_de_l%27Automobile" title="Fédération Internationale de l&#39;Automobile">FIA</a> to return.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Calendar">Calendar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2020_Formula_One_World_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Calendar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Formula_1_all_over_the_world-2020_-_current_circuits_only.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Formula_1_all_over_the_world-2020_-_current_circuits_only.svg/290px-Formula_1_all_over_the_world-2020_-_current_circuits_only.svg.png" decoding="async" width="290" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Formula_1_all_over_the_world-2020_-_current_circuits_only.svg/435px-Formula_1_all_over_the_world-2020_-_current_circuits_only.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Formula_1_all_over_the_world-2020_-_current_circuits_only.svg/580px-Formula_1_all_over_the_world-2020_-_current_circuits_only.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2754" data-file-height="1398" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Formula_1_all_over_the_world-2020_-_current_circuits_only.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Circuits originally scheduled to host a Grand Prix in 2020 are marked with a black dot.</div></div></div>
<p>Twenty-two Grands Prix were originally scheduled for the 2020 World Championship.<sup id="cite_ref-original_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-original-3">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> However, the <a href="/wiki/Impact_of_the_COVID-19_pandemic_on_sports" title="Impact of the COVID-19 pandemic on sports">COVID-19 pandemic</a> resulted in numerous race cancellations. Currently, a rescheduled calendar of seventeen races has been confirmed; twelve races have been cancelled, and one has been postponed. The length of each race is the minimum number of laps that exceeds a total distance of 305&#160;km (189.5&#160;mi). Under the sporting regulations, a minimum of eight races must take place for the season to be considered a championship.<sup id="cite_ref-wc_minimum_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wc_minimum-40">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;d&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Calendar_changes">Calendar changes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2020_Formula_One_World_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Calendar changes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After purchasing the commercial rights to the sport from <a href="/wiki/CVC_Capital_Partners" title="CVC Capital Partners">CVC Capital Partners</a> in January 2017, <a href="/wiki/Liberty_Media" title="Liberty Media">Liberty Media</a> announced plans to expand the Formula One calendar using a concept they termed "destination races" and modelled on the <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Grand_Prix" title="Singapore Grand Prix">Singapore Grand Prix</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Under the "destination races" model, Grands Prix would be established in or near key tourist destinations and integrate racing, entertainment and social functions with the aim of making the sport more accessible and appealing to a wider audience. Several countries and venues announced plans to bid for a Grand Prix,<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> with two bids being successful:
</p>
<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_Grand_Prix" title="Vietnamese Grand Prix">Vietnamese Grand Prix</a> was announced as the first new race created under Liberty's management.<sup id="cite_ref-Hanoi_announcement_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hanoi_announcement-67">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The race was given a provisional date of April 2020 and was planned to take place in the capital <a href="/wiki/Hanoi" title="Hanoi">Hanoi</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Hanoi_Street_Circuit" title="Hanoi Street Circuit">Hanoi Street Circuit</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-hanoi_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hanoi-68">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> but was later postponed.<sup id="cite_ref-BAHVIE_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BAHVIE-59">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Grand_Prix" title="Dutch Grand Prix">Dutch Grand Prix</a> was due to be revived,<sup id="cite_ref-:0_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-69">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> with the race scheduled to take place at the <a href="/wiki/Circuit_Zandvoort" title="Circuit Zandvoort">Circuit Zandvoort</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The 2020 race would have marked the first time the Dutch Grand Prix has been run since <a href="/wiki/1985_Formula_One_World_Championship" title="1985 Formula One World Championship">1985</a>. However, the race was later cancelled.<sup id="cite_ref-NED_cancelled_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NED_cancelled-72">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Liberty Media initially expected that the 2020 calendar would consist of twenty-one Grands Prix and that any new races would come at the expense of existing events, but later negotiated an agreement with the teams to allow up to twenty-two Grands Prix. Several further changes were made between the 2019 and 2020 calendars, with the <a href="/wiki/German_Grand_Prix" title="German Grand Prix">German Grand Prix</a> discontinued and the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Grand_Prix" title="Mexican Grand Prix">Mexican Grand Prix</a> rebranded as the "Mexico City Grand Prix".<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GP_lim_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GP_lim-74">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Regulation_changes">Regulation changes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2020_Formula_One_World_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Regulation changes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sporting_regulations">Sporting regulations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2020_Formula_One_World_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Sporting regulations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Teams are allowed to use an additional <a href="/wiki/Formula_One_engines" title="Formula One engines">MGU-K</a> compared to 2019 to compensate for the increased demands of contesting the originally planned twenty-two races.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:4_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-76">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Drivers who participate in free practice sessions are eligible for additional <a href="/wiki/FIA_Super_Licence" title="FIA Super Licence">FIA Super Licence</a> points. Any driver who completes a minimum 100&#160;km (62&#160;mi) during a free practice session receives an additional Super Licence point on the condition that they do not commit a driving infraction. Drivers may only accrue ten Super Licence points across a three-season period from free practice sessions.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As a result of the expanded calendar, the two pre-season tests due to take place at <a href="/wiki/Circuit_de_Barcelona-Catalunya" title="Circuit de Barcelona-Catalunya">Circuit de Barcelona-Catalunya</a> were reduced in length from four days to three days each, whilst the two in-season tests that took place at <a href="/wiki/Bahrain_International_Circuit" title="Bahrain International Circuit">Bahrain International Circuit</a> and Circuit de Barcelona-Catalunya in 2019 have been discontinued. Teams were no longer allowed to hide their cars during testing.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> The amount of time in which car mechanics are not allowed to work on the car has been extended from eight to nine hours.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-76">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The rules surrounding <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_motorsport_terms#J" title="Glossary of motorsport terms">jump starts</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Weighbridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Weighbridge">weighbridge</a> have been relaxed with the <a href="/wiki/Motorsport_marshal" title="Motorsport marshal">race stewards</a> now being able to hand out less severe punishments for missing the weighbridge and jump starts.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_76-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-76">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Technical_regulations">Technical regulations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2020_Formula_One_World_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Technical regulations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In order to reduce the risk of punctures, the last 50&#160;mm (2.0&#160;in) of the <a href="/wiki/Formula_One_car#Wings" title="Formula One car">front wing</a> can no longer contain any metal. Brake ducts can no longer be outsourced and must be made and designed by the team. The amount of fuel that can be outside of the fuel tank has been reduced from 2 litres (3.5&#160;imp&#160;pt) to 250 millilitres (0.44&#160;imp&#160;pt). The level of driver aids for race starts was decreased.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_76-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-76">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Impact_of_the_COVID-19_pandemic">Impact of the COVID-19 pandemic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2020_Formula_One_World_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Impact of the COVID-19 pandemic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Impact_of_the_COVID-19_pandemic_on_motorsport" title="Impact of the COVID-19 pandemic on motorsport">Impact of the COVID-19 pandemic on motorsport</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Initial_response">Initial response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2020_Formula_One_World_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Initial response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The season was heavily disrupted by the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>, with an announcement prior to the start of the championship that the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Grand_Prix" title="Chinese Grand Prix">Chinese Grand Prix</a> would be postponed.<sup id="cite_ref-CHN_postponed_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CHN_postponed-60">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Italian-based teams <a href="/wiki/Scuderia_Ferrari" title="Scuderia Ferrari">Ferrari</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scuderia_AlphaTauri" title="Scuderia AlphaTauri">AlphaTauri</a> expressed concern about the spread of the disease and its effect on the championship.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> As Italy suffered <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_Italy" title="COVID-19 pandemic in Italy">one of the worst outbreaks of the virus</a>, both teams were concerned about the ability of their staff to leave the quarantine zone established in northern Italy and to enter host nations. Pre-season testing in Barcelona proceeded as planned, with all teams and drivers completing the six days of testing.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ross_Brawn" title="Ross Brawn">Ross Brawn</a>, the managing director of the sport, announced that Grands Prix would not go ahead if a team were blocked from entering a host nation, but that events could go ahead if a team voluntarily chose not to enter a host nation.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> In early March, organisers of the <a href="/wiki/Bahrain_Grand_Prix" title="Bahrain Grand Prix">Bahrain Grand Prix</a> stated that the event would be "participants-only" and that no spectators would be allowed.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Race_postponements_and_cancellations">Race postponements and cancellations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2020_Formula_One_World_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Race postponements and cancellations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The season-opening <a href="/wiki/2020_Australian_Grand_Prix" title="2020 Australian Grand Prix">Australian Grand Prix</a> was expected to go ahead and all teams and drivers arrived at the venue as planned. Three days before the race was due to take place, McLaren announced their withdrawal from the event after a team member tested positive for the virus.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> This led to the Grand Prix being cancelled altogether the following morning.<sup id="cite_ref-aus_gp_off_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aus_gp_off-85">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Later that day, it was announced that the Bahrain Grand Prix would be postponed rather than closed to spectators, as would the inaugural Vietnamese Grand Prix.<sup id="cite_ref-BAHVIE_59-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BAHVIE-59">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Formula One and the <a href="/wiki/FIA" class="mw-redirect" title="FIA">FIA</a> released a joint statement saying that they "expect to begin the Championship in Europe at the end of May" but that this timeline "will be regularly reviewed".<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> On 19 March, the FIA announced that the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Grand_Prix" title="Dutch Grand Prix">Dutch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Grand_Prix" title="Spanish Grand Prix">Spanish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Monaco_Grand_Prix" title="Monaco Grand Prix">Monaco</a> Grands Prix had all been postponed indefinitely due to the pandemic. In the statement, the FIA said they now expect to begin the season "as soon as it is safe to do so after May" and that the situation would continue to be monitored.<sup id="cite_ref-NEDESPMON_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NEDESPMON-87">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The organisers of the Monaco race, Automobile Club de Monaco, clarified that the race had been cancelled. This means that Formula One would not race in Monaco for the first time since <a href="/wiki/1954_Formula_One_season" title="1954 Formula One season">1954</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Monaco_cancelled_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Monaco_cancelled-88">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Four days later, organisers of the <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Grand_Prix" title="Azerbaijan Grand Prix">Azerbaijan Grand Prix</a> announced that the race had been postponed.<sup id="cite_ref-Baku_postponed_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baku_postponed-89">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In early April, organisers of the Canadian Grand Prix announced the race's postponement.<sup id="cite_ref-CAN_postponed_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CAN_postponed-62">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Later in the month, the <a href="/wiki/French_Grand_Prix" title="French Grand Prix">French Grand Prix</a> organisers confirmed that the race would not be held in 2020,<sup id="cite_ref-FRA_cancelled_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FRA_cancelled-63">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> and the managing director of <a href="/wiki/Silverstone_Circuit" title="Silverstone Circuit">Silverstone Circuit</a> stated that should the <a href="/wiki/2020_British_Grand_Prix" title="2020 British Grand Prix">British Grand Prix</a> go ahead, it would be without spectators.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> In May, organisers of the <a href="/wiki/2020_Hungarian_Grand_Prix" title="2020 Hungarian Grand Prix">Hungarian Grand Prix</a> announced that their race would use the same model.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> The sport's plans to resume competition called for a ban on team motorhomes and a rigid testing regime to stop any outbreak of the virus.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Grand_Prix" title="Dutch Grand Prix">Dutch Grand Prix</a> was cancelled entirely in late May, with organisers of the event stating that they would prefer to host the revived race with spectators in attendance in 2021 rather than without spectators in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-NED_cancelled_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NED_cancelled-72">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Formula One confirmed the cancellation of the <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Grand_Prix" title="Azerbaijan Grand Prix">Azerbaijan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Grand_Prix" title="Singapore Grand Prix">Singapore</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Grand_Prix" title="Japanese Grand Prix">Japanese Grands Prix</a> in June.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Organisers of the Azerbaijan and Singapore races cited the difficulty of assembling the infrastructure required for a <a href="/wiki/Street_circuit" title="Street circuit">street circuit</a> as the reason for their cancellation, while the Japanese Grand Prix was cancelled because of the Japanese government's travel restrictions. In July the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Grand_Prix" title="Brazilian Grand Prix">Brazilian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Grand_Prix" title="Canadian Grand Prix">Canadian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Grand_Prix" title="Mexican Grand Prix">Mexico City</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Grand_Prix" title="United States Grand Prix">United States</a> Grands Prix were formally cancelled amidst rising virus cases and travel restrictions in <a href="/wiki/The_Americas" class="mw-redirect" title="The Americas">the Americas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> However, organisers of the Brazilian Grand Prix disputed the claims of <a href="/wiki/Formula_One_Management" class="mw-redirect" title="Formula One Management">Formula One Management</a> and were unhappy with their race being cancelled without further consultation.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> In August the cancellation of the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Grand_Prix" title="Chinese Grand Prix">Chinese Grand Prix</a> was announced.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The annual summer break, where factories shut down for two weeks, was brought forward from August to March and April. Teams nominated a three-week period to close with the aim of making room for races later in the year.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> At the end of March, it was announced that for the first time the factory shut down would additionally apply to power unit manufacturers.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-the_race_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-the_race-99">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> The factory shut down period was later extended to a total of nine weeks for competitors and seven weeks for power unit manufacturers.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rescheduled_calendar">Rescheduled calendar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2020_Formula_One_World_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Rescheduled calendar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In March, teams agreed that the 2020 Championship could run into early 2021 to ensure the running of as many races as possible. Such a move would also ensure that eight Grands Prix could be held, over three different continents, thereby meeting the minimum number of races needed for the season to qualify as a World Championship.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> Ross Brawn later suggested that a rescheduled calendar of 18 or 19 races would be possible should racing begin in July, and that the opening round "is most likely to be in Europe", potentially without spectators. He also raised the possibility of Grand Prix events being reduced to two days in order to ease pressure on logistical operations.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> However, <a href="/wiki/Alfa_Romeo_in_Formula_One" title="Alfa Romeo in Formula One">Alfa Romeo Racing</a> managing director <a href="/wiki/Fr%C3%A9d%C3%A9ric_Vasseur" title="Frédéric Vasseur">Frédéric Vasseur</a> cautioned that a condensed calendar could escalate the costs of competing and put smaller teams at risk of financial collapse.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> This was reiterated by other teams, who pointed out that the race sanctioning fees paid by event organisers contributed to the prize money awarded to all teams at the end of the year. This money is awarded proportionally based on the teams' World Constructors' Championship positions and forms a significant part of a team's budget for the upcoming year. With fewer races and the prize structure remaining fixed, teams were concerned that they would suffer a significant financial loss.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> In a statement in late April, Formula One <a href="/wiki/Chief_executive_officer" title="Chief executive officer">CEO</a> <a href="/wiki/Chase_Carey" title="Chase Carey">Chase Carey</a> announced that the intention is to begin the season on 5 July and that the target is to hold between 15 and 18 races overall.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June, the first eight races of a rescheduled calendar were confirmed, with the season expected to begin on 5 July with the <a href="/wiki/2020_Austrian_Grand_Prix" title="2020 Austrian Grand Prix">Austrian Grand Prix</a>. This revised calendar included two newly-named one-off events — both second races at the <a href="/wiki/Red_Bull_Ring" title="Red Bull Ring">Red Bull Ring</a> and <a href="/wiki/Silverstone_Circuit" title="Silverstone Circuit">Silverstone</a> — known as the <a href="/wiki/2020_Styrian_Grand_Prix" title="2020 Styrian Grand Prix">Styrian</a> and the <a href="/wiki/70th_Anniversary_Grand_Prix" title="70th Anniversary Grand Prix">70th Anniversary</a> Grands Prix respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-New_calendar_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-New_calendar-51">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Ross Brawn announced that the eight-round calendar was expected to grow and that the sport was considering races at venues that were not on the original calendar or using multiple configurations of existing circuits to achieve the goal of fifteen Grands Prix.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> On 10 July, the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Grand_Prix" title="Russian Grand Prix">Russian Grand Prix</a> was re-added to the calendar on its originally scheduled date, and the first <a href="/wiki/Tuscan_Grand_Prix" class="mw-redirect" title="Tuscan Grand Prix">Tuscan Grand Prix</a> was announced at the <a href="/wiki/Mugello_Circuit" title="Mugello Circuit">Mugello Circuit</a>, the first time the circuit will host a Formula One World Championship race.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July, the return of the <a href="/wiki/N%C3%BCrburgring" title="Nürburgring">Nürburgring</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Autodromo_Internazionale_Enzo_e_Dino_Ferrari" title="Autodromo Internazionale Enzo e Dino Ferrari">Autodromo Internazionale Enzo e Dino Ferrari</a> to the calendar was revealed, along with the debut of the <a href="/wiki/Algarve_International_Circuit" title="Algarve International Circuit">Algarve International Circuit</a>. These races were named the <a href="/wiki/Eifel_Grand_Prix" class="mw-redirect" title="Eifel Grand Prix">Eifel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Emilia_Romagna_Grand_Prix" class="mw-redirect" title="Emilia Romagna Grand Prix">Emilia Romagna</a> Grands Prix respectively, with the return of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Grand_Prix" title="Portuguese Grand Prix">Portuguese Grand Prix</a> for the first time since the <a href="/wiki/1996_Formula_One_World_Championship" title="1996 Formula One World Championship">1996</a> season. The Emilia Romagna Grand Prix will take place over a shortened two-day weekend, with a single 90 minute practice session taking place on Saturday morning.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> This marks the first race at the <a href="/wiki/N%C3%BCrburgring" title="Nürburgring">Nürburgring</a> and at the <a href="/wiki/Autodromo_Internazionale_Enzo_e_Dino_Ferrari" title="Autodromo Internazionale Enzo e Dino Ferrari">Imola Circuit</a> since the <a href="/wiki/2013_Formula_One_World_Championship" title="2013 Formula One World Championship">2013</a> and <a href="/wiki/2006_Formula_One_World_Championship" title="2006 Formula One World Championship">2006</a> seasons respectively, and also the first time that a country hosts three Grands Prix since the <a href="/wiki/1982_Formula_One_World_Championship" title="1982 Formula One World Championship">1982</a> season.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August, it was announced that Formula One would return to the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Grand_Prix" title="Turkish Grand Prix">Turkish Grand Prix</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Intercity_Istanbul_Park" title="Intercity Istanbul Park">Intercity İstanbul Park</a> for the first time since the <a href="/wiki/2011_Formula_One_World_Championship" title="2011 Formula One World Championship">2011</a> season, together with the debut of the <a href="/wiki/Sakhir_Grand_Prix" class="mw-redirect" title="Sakhir Grand Prix">Sakhir Grand Prix</a>, to be held at the <a href="/wiki/Bahrain_International_Circuit" title="Bahrain International Circuit">Bahrain International Circuit</a>, using the configuration of the track called "Outer Circuit". They join the rescheduled <a href="/wiki/Bahrain_Grand_Prix" title="Bahrain Grand Prix">Bahrain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi_Grand_Prix" title="Abu Dhabi Grand Prix">Abu Dhabi Grands Prix</a> as the final four races of the season, bringing the calendar to seventeen races.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regulatory_changes">Regulatory changes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2020_Formula_One_World_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Regulatory changes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The pandemic required changes to the format of a race weekend, which included abandoning the drivers' parade and pre-race assembly for the host venue's national anthem. A modified podium ceremony was planned for after races.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> The FIA introduced limits to the number of team personnel who could be on the starting grid to prepare cars and changed the cut-off times for cars to leave pit lane to minimise the amount of time team personnel spent on the grid.<sup id="cite_ref-covid_grid_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-covid_grid-117">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Tyre supplier <a href="/wiki/Pirelli" title="Pirelli">Pirelli</a> was also required to provide an identical allocation of tyre compounds to all teams and drivers. Where Pirelli were previously required to announce compounds for a race several weeks in advance, this window was reduced to two weeks, allowing them to respond to anticipated changes to the calendar.<sup id="cite_ref-covid_grid_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-covid_grid-117">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Solidarity_campaign">Solidarity campaign</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2020_Formula_One_World_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Solidarity campaign">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In June, Formula One launched the <i>We Race As One</i> initiative to fight racism, global inequity and the impact of COVID-19. The initiative used a rainbow logo, with the #WeRaceAsOne hashtag, and featured prominent <i>We Race As One</i> branding on vehicles (including the safety car) and signage on track. Formula One and several teams launched projects or fundraising efforts in support of the initiative.<sup id="cite_ref-F1com-20200622_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-F1com-20200622-118">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Autosport-20200622_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Autosport-20200622-119">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Protests_against_car_legality">Protests against car legality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2020_Formula_One_World_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Protests against car legality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mercedes">Mercedes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2020_Formula_One_World_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Mercedes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Ahead of the season opening <a href="/wiki/2020_Austrian_Grand_Prix" title="2020 Austrian Grand Prix">Austrian Grand Prix</a>, <a href="/wiki/Red_Bull_Racing" title="Red Bull Racing">Red Bull</a> launched a protest against the <a href="/wiki/Mercedes_F1_W11" class="mw-redirect" title="Mercedes F1 W11">Mercedes F1 W11</a>'s dual axis steering – a system where the driver can adjust the <a href="/wiki/Toe_(automotive)" title="Toe (automotive)">toe</a> of the car by pulling and pushing on the steering wheel. The system was found to be legal for 2020, but it would be banned by the FIA from 2021 onward.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Racing_Point">Racing Point</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2020_Formula_One_World_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Racing Point">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/2020_Styrian_Grand_Prix" title="2020 Styrian Grand Prix">Styrian Grand Prix</a>, <a href="/wiki/Renault_F1" class="mw-redirect" title="Renault F1">Renault</a> launched a protest against the brake ducts of <a href="/wiki/Racing_Point_F1_Team" title="Racing Point F1 Team">Racing Point</a>'s car, the <a href="/wiki/Racing_Point_RP20" title="Racing Point RP20">RP20</a>, alleging that Racing Point had copied the brake ducts from the <a href="/wiki/Mercedes_F1_W10" class="mw-redirect" title="Mercedes F1 W10">Mercedes F1 W10</a> – the car used in 2019 by <a href="/wiki/Mercedes_F1" class="mw-redirect" title="Mercedes F1">Mercedes</a>. Similar protests would be launched after the <a href="/wiki/2020_Hungarian_Grand_Prix" title="2020 Hungarian Grand Prix">Hungarian</a> and <a href="/wiki/2020_British_Grand_Prix" title="2020 British Grand Prix">British Grands Prix</a> with the verdict being published between the British and <a href="/wiki/70th_Anniversary_Grand_Prix" title="70th Anniversary Grand Prix">70th Anniversary Grands Prix</a>. The ruling concluded that <a href="/wiki/Racing_Point_F1_Team" title="Racing Point F1 Team">Racing Point</a> had illegally copied the brake ducts of the Mercedes F1 W10 and Racing Point were subsequently penalised by 15 Constructors' Championship points and fined <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">€</a>400,000.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Racing Point, <a href="/wiki/Scuderia_Ferrari" title="Scuderia Ferrari">Ferrari</a>, <a href="/wiki/McLaren" title="McLaren">McLaren</a>, Renault and <a href="/wiki/Williams_Grand_Prix_Engineering" title="Williams Grand Prix Engineering">Williams</a> had all indicated an intention to appeal the stewards decision with Racing Point trying to clear their name and Ferrari, McLaren, Williams and Renault appealing for a tougher sanction.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Ferrari, Renault and Racing Point confirmed their appeal, while Williams and McLaren pulled out of the appeal.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Later, Renault announced their decision to withdraw the appeal against the penalty handed out to Racing Point.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> The same decision was made by Racing Point and Ferrari before and after the <a href="/wiki/2020_Italian_Grand_Prix" title="2020 Italian Grand Prix">Italian Grand Prix</a> respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_summary">Season summary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2020_Formula_One_World_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Season summary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Opening_rounds">Opening rounds</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2020_Formula_One_World_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Opening rounds">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The delayed season started with the <a href="/wiki/2020_Austrian_Grand_Prix" title="2020 Austrian Grand Prix">Austrian Grand Prix</a>. <a href="/wiki/Valtteri_Bottas" title="Valtteri Bottas">Valtteri Bottas</a>, driving for <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_in_Formula_One" title="Mercedes-Benz in Formula One">Mercedes</a>, took <a href="/wiki/Pole_position" title="Pole position">pole position</a>, ahead of his teammate <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Hamilton" title="Lewis Hamilton">Lewis Hamilton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Red_Bull_Racing" title="Red Bull Racing">Red Bull</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Max_Verstappen" title="Max Verstappen">Max Verstappen</a>; however, Hamilton was given a three-place grid penalty, since he did not slow sufficiently when yellow flags were waved following a small mistake by Bottas. This promoted Verstappen to second, <a href="/wiki/McLaren" title="McLaren">McLaren</a> driver <a href="/wiki/Lando_Norris" title="Lando Norris">Lando Norris</a> to third, and <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Albon" title="Alexander Albon">Alexander Albon</a> to fourth. In an eventful race, featuring three safety car periods and the retirements of nine drivers, Bottas won, ahead of the <a href="/wiki/Scuderia_Ferrari" title="Scuderia Ferrari">Ferrari</a> of <a href="/wiki/Charles_Leclerc" title="Charles Leclerc">Charles Leclerc</a> and Norris. Hamilton crossed the line in second place, but received a five-second time penalty after a collision with Albon, who soon retired; after the penalty was applied, Hamilton finished fourth, ahead of <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Sainz_Jr." title="Carlos Sainz Jr.">Carlos Sainz Jr.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sergio_P%C3%A9rez" title="Sergio Pérez">Sergio Pérez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Gasly" title="Pierre Gasly">Pierre Gasly</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/2020_Styrian_Grand_Prix" title="2020 Styrian Grand Prix">Styrian Grand Prix</a> was won by Hamilton ahead of Bottas and <a href="/wiki/Max_Verstappen" title="Max Verstappen">Max Verstappen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/2020_Hungarian_Grand_Prix" title="2020 Hungarian Grand Prix">Hungarian Grand Prix</a> started with a slippery track. Verstappen slid into the barrier on his way to the grid and broke his steering axis, but his mechanics managed to repair the car before the race start. The race winner was Hamilton, with Verstappen in second and Bottas in third place.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Hamilton won the <a href="/wiki/2020_British_Grand_Prix" title="2020 British Grand Prix">British Grand Prix</a> despite his left-front tyre delaminating in the middle of the last lap. Verstappen finished second with Leclerc in third.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> Bottas had a puncture which resulted in him finishing in eleventh. <a href="/wiki/Daniil_Kvyat" title="Daniil Kvyat">Daniil Kvyat</a> had a puncture at high speed entering Maggotts corner which resulted in a big crash with a safety car, and <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Sainz_Jr." title="Carlos Sainz Jr.">Carlos Sainz Jr.</a> finished 13th after a puncture made him fall from what would have been 4th place.
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/70th_Anniversary_Grand_Prix" title="70th Anniversary Grand Prix">70th Anniversary Grand Prix</a>, Verstappen won with Hamilton second and Bottas third. This was the first non-Mercedes win of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/2020_Spanish_Grand_Prix" title="2020 Spanish Grand Prix">Spanish Grand Prix</a> was won by Hamilton with Verstappen in second and Bottas in third.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mid-season_rounds">Mid-season rounds</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2020_Formula_One_World_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Mid-season rounds">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/2020_Belgian_Grand_Prix" title="2020 Belgian Grand Prix">Belgian Grand Prix</a> was won by <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Hamilton" title="Lewis Hamilton">Lewis Hamilton</a>, who led every lap and won by 8 seconds over teammate <a href="/wiki/Valtteri_Bottas" title="Valtteri Bottas">Valtteri Bottas</a> who finished second ahead of <a href="/wiki/Max_Verstappen" title="Max Verstappen">Max Verstappen</a>. <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Ricciardo" title="Daniel Ricciardo">Daniel Ricciardo</a> finished fourth, setting the fastest lap on the last lap. On lap 11, <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Giovinazzi" title="Antonio Giovinazzi">Antonio Giovinazzi</a> crashed at Campus corner; one of the wheels of his car came loose and hit the front right suspension of <a href="/wiki/George_Russell_(racing_driver)" title="George Russell (racing driver)">George Russell</a>’s car, causing both drivers to retire from the race. This brought out the safety car for three laps. <a href="/wiki/Renault_in_Formula_One" title="Renault in Formula One">Renault</a> achieved a finish of P4 and P5, equalling their best result since their return to the sport in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/2020_Italian_Grand_Prix" title="2020 Italian Grand Prix">Italian Grand Prix</a> was won by <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Gasly" title="Pierre Gasly">Pierre Gasly</a> after a <a href="/wiki/Red_flag_(racing)" class="mw-redirect" title="Red flag (racing)">red flag</a> caused by <a href="/wiki/Charles_Leclerc" title="Charles Leclerc">Charles Leclerc</a>. This was his and <a href="/wiki/Scuderia_AlphaTauri" title="Scuderia AlphaTauri">AlphaTauri</a>'s first race victory. The race marked the first time since <a href="/wiki/Kimi_R%C3%A4ikk%C3%B6nen" title="Kimi Räikkönen">Kimi Räikkönen</a> won the <a href="/wiki/2013_Australian_Grand_Prix" title="2013 Australian Grand Prix">2013 Australian Grand Prix</a> driving for <a href="/wiki/Lotus_F1" title="Lotus F1">Lotus F1</a> that the race winner did not drive for <a href="/wiki/Scuderia_Ferrari" title="Scuderia Ferrari">Ferrari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_in_Formula_One" title="Mercedes-Benz in Formula One">Mercedes</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Red_Bull_Racing" title="Red Bull Racing">Red Bull</a> and the first time since <a href="/wiki/2012_Hungarian_Grand_Prix" title="2012 Hungarian Grand Prix">2012 Hungarian Grand Prix</a> these all of these three constructors failed to score a podium finish. The race marked the second career podium finishes for <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Sainz_Jr." title="Carlos Sainz Jr.">Carlos Sainz Jr.</a>, who finished second, and <a href="/wiki/Lance_Stroll" title="Lance Stroll">Lance Stroll</a>, who finished third.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The inaugural <a href="/wiki/2020_Tuscan_Grand_Prix" title="2020 Tuscan Grand Prix">Tuscan Grand Prix</a>, Ferrari's 1000th Grand Prix start, resulted in Hamilton's sixth race win of the season, and Mercedes' third 1-2 finish. Bottas overtook Hamilton into turn one before a major collision at turn two caused the retirement of both Verstappen (who had fallen from 3rd to 14th due to a power issue) and Gasly. This brought out the safety car for 8 laps to allow for the debris to be cleared. At the end of the safety car period, a major misunderstanding in the upper midfield led to a large collision down the pit straight, causing the retirement of <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Latifi" title="Nicholas Latifi">Nicholas Latifi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Magnussen" title="Kevin Magnussen">Kevin Magnussen</a>, Giovinazzi and Sainz Jr., and a red flag period. At the first restart, Hamilton overtook Bottas and led the race from there onwards. On lap 42, Ricciardo looked poised for his first podium since the <a href="/wiki/2018_Monaco_Grand_Prix" title="2018 Monaco Grand Prix">2018 Monaco Grand Prix</a> when Stroll's <a href="/wiki/Racing_Point_F1_Team" title="Racing Point F1 Team">Racing Point</a> spun off the track due to a <a href="/wiki/Flat_tire" title="Flat tire">puncture</a>, causing the second red flag of the race. This was the first time since the <a href="/wiki/2016_Brazilian_Grand_Prix" title="2016 Brazilian Grand Prix">2016 Brazilian Grand Prix</a> that there were two red flag periods in one race. At the second restart, Hamilton maintained his lead to win the race. <a href="/wiki/Red_Bull_Racing" title="Red Bull Racing">Red Bull's</a> <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Albon" title="Alexander Albon">Alexander Albon</a> overtook Ricciardo in the closing laps, earning his first ever podium, and the first podium for a <a href="/wiki/Formula_One_drivers_from_Thailand" title="Formula One drivers from Thailand">Thai driver in Formula One</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Results_and_standings">Results and standings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2020_Formula_One_World_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Results and standings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scoring_system">Scoring system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2020_Formula_One_World_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Scoring system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Formula_One_World_Championship_points_scoring_systems" title="List of Formula One World Championship points scoring systems">List of Formula One World Championship points scoring systems</a></div>
<p>Points are awarded to the top ten classified drivers and the driver who set the fastest lap. The driver with the fastest lap has to be within the top 10 to receive the point. The points are awarded for every race using the following system:<sup id="cite_ref-points_regs_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-points_regs-137">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2020_Formula_One_World_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r936637989">.mw-parser-output .portal{border:solid #aaa 1px;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .portal.tleft{margin:0.5em 1em 0.5em 0}.mw-parser-output .portal.tright{margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul{display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li{display:table-row}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li>span:first-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li>span:last-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle}</style><div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright">
<ul>
<li><span><a href="/wiki/File:Motorsport_current_event.svg" class="image"><img alt="icon" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Motorsport_current_event.svg/28px-Motorsport_current_event.svg.png" decoding="async" width="28" height="28" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Motorsport_current_event.svg/42px-Motorsport_current_event.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Motorsport_current_event.svg/56px-Motorsport_current_event.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="400" /></a></span><span><a href="/wiki/Portal:Formula_One" title="Portal:Formula One">Formula One portal</a></span></li></ul></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/2020_Formula_One_pre-season_testing" title="2020 Formula One pre-season testing">2020 Formula One pre-season testing</a></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2020_Formula_One_World_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Formula_One" title="History of Formula One">history of Formula One</a>, Formula One regulations were first introduced during the <a href="/wiki/1946_Grand_Prix_season" title="1946 Grand Prix season">1946 Grand Prix season</a>. These were adopted for every race in <a href="/wiki/1948_Grand_Prix_season" title="1948 Grand Prix season">1948</a>, and were formally organised into a championship in 1950.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-21"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-21">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Racing Point F1 Team uses Mercedes-AMG F1 M11 power units. For sponsorship purposes, these engines are rebadged as "<a href="/wiki/BWT_AG" title="BWT AG">BWT</a> Mercedes".<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-22">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Sergio_P%C3%A9rez" title="Sergio Pérez">Sergio Pérez</a> was entered into the <a href="/wiki/2020_British_Grand_Prix" title="2020 British Grand Prix">2020 British Grand Prix</a>, but later withdrew after testing positive for the <a href="/wiki/Severe_acute_respiratory_syndrome_coronavirus_2" title="Severe acute respiratory syndrome coronavirus 2">SARS-2 coronavirus</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-43"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-43">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Under the FIA's International Sporting Code,  a season must contest races across three continents to be considered a World Championship.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-44"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-44">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Hungarian Grand Prix was originally due to take place on 2 August, but was rescheduled due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_Hungary" title="COVID-19 pandemic in Hungary">COVID-19 pandemic</a>, replacing the British Grand Prix race date.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-45"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-45">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The British Grand Prix was originally due to take place on 19 July, but was rescheduled due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="COVID-19 pandemic in the United Kingdom">COVID-19 pandemic</a>, replacing the Hungarian Grand Prix race date.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-46"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-46">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Spanish Grand Prix was originally due to take place on 10 May, but was rescheduled due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_Spain" title="COVID-19 pandemic in Spain">COVID-19 pandemic</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-47"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-47">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The circuit is subject to passing <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9d%C3%A9ration_Internationale_de_l%27Automobile" title="Fédération Internationale de l&#39;Automobile">FIA</a> homologation inspection.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-48"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-48">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Bahrain Grand Prix will be run using the traditional layout called "Grand Prix Circuit", while the Sakhir Grand Prix will be run using a different layout called "Outer Circuit".</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-49"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-49">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Bahrain Grand Prix was originally due to take place on 22 March, but was rescheduled due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_Bahrain" title="COVID-19 pandemic in Bahrain">COVID-19 pandemic</a>, replacing the Abu Dhabi Grand Prix race date.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-50"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-50">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Abu Dhabi Grand Prix was originally due to take place on 29 November, but was rescheduled due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="COVID-19 pandemic in the United Arab Emirates">COVID-19 pandemic</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-AUS_status-57"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-AUS_status_57-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a href="/wiki/2020_Australian_Grand_Prix" title="2020 Australian Grand Prix">Australian Grand Prix</a> was cancelled due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_Australia" title="COVID-19 pandemic in Australia">COVID-19 pandemic</a>, but organisers announced their intention to reschedule the race.<sup id="cite_ref-ausTBA_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ausTBA-55">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Federal tourism minister <a href="/wiki/Simon_Birmingham" title="Simon Birmingham">Simon Birmingham</a> later stated his belief that Australia's borders would be closed to international travel until 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-VIE_status-58"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-VIE_status_58-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Despite confirmation that the 2020 championship will have 17 Grands Prix, there has not been any formal announcement of the cancellation of the Vietnamese Grand Prix.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-RP_points-140"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-RP_points_140-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Racing_Point_F1_Team" title="Racing Point F1 Team">Racing Point</a> drivers scored 107 points, but the constructor was deducted 15 points after a protest from <a href="/wiki/Renault_in_Formula_One" title="Renault in Formula One">Renault</a> was upheld regarding the legality of <a href="/wiki/Racing_Point_RP20" title="Racing Point RP20">their car</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
